O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, my dear children, I have completed this book which is the compendium of medical knowledge and its conclusion through explanations and statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me that I have completed this work with the treatment in question, which is derived from manual labor, namely "civil surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because manual labor is prevalent in our region and is essential everywhere, it enables the practice of science to progress rapidly, without any delay for obtaining knowledge contained only briefly within ancient books that hands have written.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes confusion and pride, leading to closed minds about the field of study; knowledge becomes isolated as a result.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems I will revive this treatment together according to the path of exposure and explanation, and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I will come together the forms of fire cupping and other tools from iron with the assistance in setting up these things; so it is for a skilled person.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no master craftsmen of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And those who enter into this must study the science of anatomy as Galen says, grasping firmly in mind the judgment of bodies, and their forms and connections and separations within them; understanding bones, nerves, arteries and veins, movement and rest periods, and so on.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this disease wherein he speaks of Ipse who is without manure (implying a lack of beneficial substances), and with the urine is potent.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and immediately in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not conscious of what has been said before and does not lie or deceive humans.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	I have often wanted many of these who intercede in this art and abandon it, leaving themselves without its knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	I see a madman who fashions an abscess or the neck of a woman and cuts into the arteries there.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For moisture, so much blood is out of place that a dead woman's flesh lies between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And another view which betrays an arrow from ancient wood, and the arrow was large.
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	If it carried away a part of the bladder, and died within three years.

et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant mind squeezes breakthroughs at wounds by strong force, leaving no room in the injury for healing to occur and leaves it incomplete as soon as possible.

Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take quicklime and hot chalk together, grind them all in one piece, then place the mixture into a new vessel.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	When it has no small opening through which the point of an arrow may pass.
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and fills it with another pot well-plumbed, and put on alkaline earth or chalky substance along with gentle powder above them until he has two of such at the top.
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Let it be left so long as he expels phlegm and blood or pus; then take all the effusion, and cast it into lime and alkali as is done beforehand.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And when there will be blood in flux from medicinal ointments and other treatments.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	In its work as we do with honey and wax using soap, all these things together mix well.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galens tells of a treatment for the pain in the hip and sciatic nerve, which was his main course; he said that no other remedy sufficed them, and they were cured once when this measure was taken, after which they bathed as instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And he directs that you grind the fresh and dry litargy into powder, crush it with a spoonful of fatty substance, apply to the hip joint and thigh where pain holds on, rubbing in the mixture.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he leaves it for three hours according to the quantity so that the patient does not feel any pain anymore.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then he makes him enter the bath until his joint is loosened up, and into a bed wherein his pain will go away completely and be cleansed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And none shall use such treatments without first evacuating pus.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Diadochus says that when the sciatic nerve is cauterized with lamb's fleece wool, if it helps;
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and must make those burns according to manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and honeyed oil, and place them on the indentation between the thumb bone (pis) and the other called socket (foscile).  
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After taking fir branches, and carrying into the fire until they become charcoal, place them on wool, and leave them as long as they are glowing.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and continue doing so again and again until you use your judgment to think it wanes as for the shoulder blade and that the pain goes away.
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	And this method of fire cupping is called "firecupping".

de la dolor des jointes	of pain from the joints

et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the arrows used to examine sorcerers' bones and come in copper-colored or iron ones, valued more than yellow needles for sealing abscesses with black plugs.
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three methods;
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, moisture-related, small, according to the quantity of secretions produced by the wound or abscess.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of owlets are like oxen shapes as you see here.

et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	And if they are one-eyed with two horns, and half an eye within the same ones; of three kinds.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and these things are necessary in their flesh.

des apostemes des asselles	of arrows' incisions or punctures
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These are joints of bones that come from the shoulders and contain moisture within them.

de la routure de l’artere	From the cautery of the artery

et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And secure the instrument's size to that of your hand if you find it necessary for an extension tool in all parts of the skin. des apostemes des ners	of abscess drains
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Ash come out in the artery and vein, they come out when it dies from too much labor or similar things.

des grosses boces pendans	large jaws dangling downwards.

et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient fearful about the incision with iron, take a strong thread as we have said, and in it leave him for days.

quant li boude ist fuer	when the bite is for
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	when the bite appears due to a wound cautery or fracture of flesh, and is located in the abdomen and elsewhere on the body, if it comes from blood draining through veins or arteries as dictated by what's ahead, or from wind troubles;

(Note: The phrase 'moitiety' likely means half, referring here possibly to partaking in some formative or preparatory action.)

dou chancre	Deal with ulcers accordingly to address them effectively for
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have discussed the similarities of ulcers and how they should be treated with medicine, as well as commenting on whether we must apply a poultice made from iron. (Note: The original Old French text appears to touch upon treatments for wounds potentially involving metal pewter or "fer" in medieval times.)
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	And let us declare the ulcer manifest in skin and heavy cure is needed therein, as well as onset of chancres when they are lodged or can be drawn out like a chancre present within milkmaids' breasts and nipples, and also in other similar lesions; which must all be removed at the earliest stage.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	And when it is large and ancient, there's no need for immediate intervention beyond gentle approach since I will never find a cure.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	Never before has any been healed by me.

puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then let the healer make him lie down if there is evident swelling, then lift his leg for doing the work.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then pluck out warts or sores from all over and cut the hair everywhere without leaving anything behind.

puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply further treatment until he is healthy again.
de ydropisie	of dropsy (historically referring to edema
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division of these dropsy types that water is collected and how its signs are assembled; concerning medicine treatments for each type, as well as those treated with iron. (Note: This translation attempts to maintain the original meaning while converting Old French medieval terminology into modern English where possible.)
si est eclites soulement;	if it is broken down by moisture or fluid retention in parts of the body causing

c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	it is known that it concerns the deadly types: tympanites and hydrocele because they are fatal matters. (Tympanites refers to bladder stones affecting fluid-filled areas of the body like ears or sinuses, while ypos
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	When you apply this medicine's appearance of jaundice ("yellowing"), and the cure does not benefit if you observe that your patients are weak or have other diseases besides jaundice, such as indigestion with its remedy for stomach issues and similar things.
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if it is not touched by iron, because they have doubts about it.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient with great resolve and no other illness but drowning solely, and not excessively thin or fat, then in this way act upon them.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Pray the patient to hold his hands up and let them press downwards at the lowest part of his belly; then take the sharp-spined thorn in this manner.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so they are torn apart by two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	And so they are torn apart by two points. And let nothing enter it once pinned down and fixed therein, nor be cleaved with a sharp instrument.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	Then look for signs of inflammation towards the intestines.
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If you find that there is more froth in third portion upwards, straighten out those pains above it.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	And if the inflammation is due to liver disease, then your incision should be made on the right side of the third portion.

de la routure dou syfac	from the rush of blood (implied by context)
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The dislocation here occurs through the cutting or extension into the abdomen in the groin area, causing the intestines to stretch from their usual position.

des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said concerning wound treatment.
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	Or you shall speak of hands and medicines according to their fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to how they are made; and in accordance with the type of injury or where it is caused—from here onward considering these aspects as well-made criteria for treatment.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things concerning injuries are made by the grinding of bone and sharpness of spear tip or arrowheads, crossbow bolts, cannonballs, javelins, darts, lances, arrows—and similar objects.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or they are made according to the types of wounds caused on the neck, head (or top), shoulder blade(s), chest, liver and other joint-like parts—and similar body segments.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you how to treat some wounds and begin at simple sore parts since the memory of this chapter comes with it.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	Whenever a simple wound or injury occurs and the bone is not fractured, if you notice it's from slipping of joint or similar things, where the leather has been torn all over, and you have slight feverish sweating fear:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	If he makes a sudden attempt to move his head if there comes forth blood from the wound and it is moved contrary to its normal part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	Let them consume wine and heavy meats.

et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And apply salve to the wound, with a piece of cloth impregnated in rosy oil or exact wine solution.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if the wound does not heat up naturally or is fresh with all its blood, and it moves because of air or dust particles only then I shall mention one point after.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the arrow has moved within him, let them apply some salves on it until he is cleansed or healthy again.

et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and if they possess medicine for the treatment of medicines' decay caused by cure processes, and do not benefit unless it covers that limb until corrosion comes forth or death approaches due to negligence—that is a greater threat than failure in treating the body part; whereby patients might face mortality directly as they seek help. This passage conveys urgency for using protective measures against further damage and emphasizes how critical it can be when medical intervention fails, potentially leading to death either through neglect or external negligence referred to here with ‘malice’ which is described as a greater threat than physical treatment failure (‘defaute dou membre’).
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and when the signs show that the limb appears blackened as if it were charred by fire, after turning black, take up those burns on the body and touch them with every part of one's own flesh.

Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The salts that come together for necessity arise naturally or from wound healing, burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you cover it with a plasterer, then they must restore according to their natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two fine linens or cloths soaked in rose oil that they do not heal.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Place thin wooden pegs between them so long as the bones are set, if that is what he intends to do.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	It comes to no one of its due with the palm if it is so much as needed for salt. (Note: This sentence appears metaphorical or symbolic in nature and may require interpretation within a broader context.)

Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment of iron follows two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is where they draw blood, and bleed black venom.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way if you bind the vein entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size should be according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Rises first the arm of hot water strong enough that it does not subtly withdraw from him/her. Then stretch (or strain) the leg downward for the patient, up to just below the knee joint on their thigh side until they begin to open or loosen;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then bind the vein with one or two large knots (first to second joint below knee on thigh side), and drain out black venom from your hand, moving from one chief to another as long as much fluid remains in him/her until their vital force can no longer bear it;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then comes the blood, and he commands him to dress it with black meat.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Repeat evacuation and sanitation when wounds are bandaged, and attend the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The handling of it is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	The treatment involves the leg of the patient being carried if it has hair, then placed in water or washed and their injured limb is immersed in hot water until it turns red and swollen. (Please note that this translation may not fully capture the original intent due to ambiguities inherent in medieval texts.)
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if there is no bath available, then heat the wound fire and apply it to where long hair adorns the head or down by the ankle. (As with previous translations, some interpretation may be required due to archaic language.)
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then apply pressure to the wound, and scrape the vein in some parts until it feels.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when she appears red and black like a frayed sinew;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then thrusts into place the razor so that it is covered with leather, and then straightens out one knot above three others.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Scrub the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it upwards like you have done before, and secure with another pin if necessary.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then take another size up if you are skilled at it, then lubricate and cut with two pieces of wood, then treat and lift as for the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract in sizes until she yields completely, then shape it again with two pieces of wood to cut it further.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot extract and raise her at all, insert a strong sharp needle into every fiber tightly bound together. Then pull out (and lift) it alternately with one hand on each side until she yields completely.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep her in place because if it moves again (after being extracted), she cannot be pulled out or raised anymore, and becomes detrimental to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have treated it all, apply linen soaked in wine and oil rose to the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and continue until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if it's twisted and bent together like we said, you must break them apart forcefully but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat as directed before by us.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	And if it's the form of iron where we coat (break) a vein, and do not cut it anymore. de la voinne civile	of a civilian woman (implied by context)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This branch is growing on its legs in hot parts where neither grass nor tree grows, and there's no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And it also grows elsewhere than on its legs, and this parasite comes from the skin like fleas in goat feet and ticks between leather and cloth.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if it is that there comes a great inflammation in the leg, then they bind their feet and start this parasite growing outwardly, as when a root of a plant grows upwards.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head is opened, they must wrap it tightly with a piece of wood about halfway from one inch to two inches around the leg. They leave this bandage on until each time when they need to relieve themselves and then remove the wrapping along with new growth or regeneration;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it and wrap the wrapping around removing only from its root until it has entirely come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	if you manage it, then enters into flesh, bringing forth abscess and putrefaction or the lead (implying metal foreign bodies), worsening of illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this matter it must be treated quickly and thoroughly, leaving no trace or sinew.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And never has this vein been treated by the five hands of length or more, and some knights came to me, who stood on it with limbs spanning out for lengths X, and when I touched her, if any rope or thorns were there, they would bounce up immediately; thus she persists in issuing.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	Let it be drained of its material inside, and bring to the patient medicine through digestion without fail each day until healed as with pills.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	Never under any circumstances at this vein, and immediately when it opens at the joint or bone, where there is a fracture coming loose;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure him as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that grow between hide and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is present in our land as the "cattle sickness," because it often occurs from worms (bou) and is a small worm that lives between hide and flesh. It moves throughout the body entering and exiting tendons and muscles, causing severe pain at every joint until it leaves either through skin or by hopping;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is invaded by some humor, just like worms and lice and roundworms enter the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And if one doubts its malignity, for when it goes through the body and ascends to the head, and comes upon fat, by chance enters, and ruins the fat;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see and treat it, if there is pain only when he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	When you lie the joint above and below a strong ligament tightly, then apply pressure on it and treat with force, and direct it towards the flesh where it penetrates deeply; do not prevent its healing if cauterized by fire until it dries up.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And if it causes such great harm as we have said when it rubs oil.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see him coming or head pressing from the oils, then strain on them and treat accordingly.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And the patient must use purifying agents of medicine for removing impurities from corrupted fluids and consume meats in their raw state (raw meat).
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from wind inflammation.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is prevalent in our land "to spread", and it's pain that affects any limb, moving from one member to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I see you believe this too.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a woman healer (or female doctor), where I found my arm swollen in the vein.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and then he placed it there as quickly as possible, using live silver (or fresh metal) whenever needed.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain left the one in use and focused on the shoulder blade, coming back to the other arm repeatedly.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that it twisted around inside the joint like I was watching her do so.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I reeled it up as best I could in response to her movements of this limb-on-limb manner because I had never seen such a sickness beforehand. Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Always I have wanted to move the pain from one joint to another, but I never did see it in a woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because women had dry skin and exposed veins, and by that appeared the wind-constrained movement.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it is not according to this reason for those who are delightful and have moist skin and renewed veins.

des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their shapes and sizes of joints or where they prick.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Its variety consists that it has those with large points, and small ones, beards, curls;  
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those with two joints, and on those who have tongues, and on those that have parts.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And those who hurt any part of their body according to these two ways.
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	And those who hurt the head of their member similarly to brain, liver, gallbladder (cholecyst), spleen, bowels, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	And when they harm none of these members without cause, and the sign of death appears to me then I will tell you what it is afterward.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If they wish that you labor at extracting this arrowhead for the fact that death comes after in various ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if this bad sign does not appear to you either and the arrowhead is yet intact, then cut through it (and treat the wound).
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign when an arrow pierces and penetrates the bone, and his tongue snaps back where it is attached to the brain stem (medulla oblongata), such as blinding darkness and weakness upward and downward in them, inflammation of the throat, spasm of understanding, vomiting from the colon;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And through lack of nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And possibly affecting speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And from the wet ulcer looking like poultice, and it smells as if of burning charcoal.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And when signs appear to you in the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not entangled within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the shoulder when it feels cold or numb is that it presses against the left breastbone and senses as if frozen in a hard object, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the shoulder becomes mute like a chicken, and brings forth black blood with cold sweat, leading to shivering and potential fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore it gives reason for doubt that there is death involved.

The sign of the arrowhead that is not visible upon touching it is when without wound scabs it jumps from the injury site and the throat swells; patients' limbs turn a different color and suddenly hoarsen, suspecting cold drafts entering their bodies.

Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I placed the cautery on my hands all year round, and healed his wound quickly, and kept them long so that the patient felt the arrow in his knee each day.
et il le me dist.	and he gives it to me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied it to the wound with hands during wintertime until it was gone, and I tried, feeling the head of the arrowhead as it lifted up in the lymph.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then insert into the wound with that medicinal blood until the arrowhead becomes clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and thoroughly covers it for three months, and then I extracted the arrowheads with pliers on both sides, but could not remove them.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I continued to carefully manipulate and adjust with tweezers for a whole day using well-made pliers as per the guidance of this chapter until it was done, and then I would seal up the wound again.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And he judged that neither nasal congestion could be restored in him.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Therefore, I sealed up the wound again and it healed my patients entirely cleanly.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	You have described the quality of extracting any arrows, since you cannot grasp everything as books can't comprehend it all.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the greatest masters use nine times more effort and new instruments for extracting foreign objects encountered in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows are inserted or fixed into the limbs only according to two methods:  
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Or when they enter by way of their joint or otherwise.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which jumps through the limb enters into its fleshly joint; it has never done so before.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if she does not now jump, as long as the limb is moistened and agitated within her body, and until the cause of this dislocation emerges.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if she is fixed in the bone and cannot move outward hereafter unless each day there is some movement of her limb.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she jumps again, and if not, whenever there is any subtle motion beneath her fleshly joint until the lubrication within it expands; then treat her limb accordingly.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes into one of the sides of the brain, among the accidents I have mentioned to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you do not remove it, but leave it so long after any seasons have passed, for the arrow comes just as if by sinew or tendon; that is when death occurs.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the arrow is lodged only in bone and does not come by sinew or tendon, and causes no discomfort to the patient for any length of time before removal, then death will result from removing it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if she is deeply lodged and cannot be drawn out, then I apply cauterizing tools as previously mentioned.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the limb until it is cleaned.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if you cannot see its socket in place there, fear not the instrument has returned to its joint.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you sense it without any tool capable of conveying.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot by the severity of the wound or through arrows' sharpness and lacking any bone nor sinew to heal it until the injury is great.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and remove the arrow if you can take it out and if there are ears attached to it in the shaft where bone fragments remain from two parts upwards that you have removed so far, then break or fold down the ears of the arrowhead as much as possible while extracting.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and handle it carefully without breaking the arrowhead further; remove it more cautiously.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it even once, continue until the head is down to its roots; removal then becomes laborious and arduous work.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding continues while you are moving it, contradict what we have stated in this chapter about treatment. et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And guard the incision in the nerve and vein, and apply as you pull out the arrowhead or spear, either quickly or slowly, tightly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And place the patient according to their original shape when the arrow falls on them, for it is the greatest help that they can have, and if you cannot do so, then follow what signs show upon thee.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or it has nothing to do with him, or the skin feels inflamed where you see or sense it.

si saut fuer maintenant.	if he jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, twist your round hand so long as it enters the bone, and expands the bone, then pull out (or extract).
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot remove it, let her continue to hold on until it exudes force.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if it is of arrowheads throughout its entire length.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if it was cut, and you see to administer bandaging, provided that the arrowhead of your instrument enters into the hair of the tool.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then throw it outwards, and so is its instrument sharply entering within, to aid in the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, they must cover all thatched or leather wherein the poison may be contained; when you can handle it safely, then treat the wound as best one could manage to contain and neutralize it.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow pierces or falls upon the breastbone or bladder and is freshly inserted, then you may cover it over there.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And avoid covering the vein and nerve, then extract it, and afterwards suture the wound, which is what skilled work entails.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and so long as she remains healthy.

de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of books

Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Due moisture prompts movement, hastening fractures more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And remember that bones of the old and brittle cannot be well restored or mended according to their natural state, nor by those who are too tender as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But without care, reset the bone fragment that breaks and joins together all at once as if it had been before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And not one part of his work is spared, and for this reason he must consume large amounts of meat as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And that fractures occur in various ways through many methods.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of a joint is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all methods for breaking in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	And there is a fracture when it goes to war and another by sharpening, similar to the size of a writing quill that he has cut himself with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with wound, and a crack all over one small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at times he should have his tool with him, and its proper instrument for restoration according to what comes into his mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And when the bone is broken by what comes into his mind, and it's properly opened up with forceps in hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when it does not have twistiness or the patient feels no great pain, there is no breakage.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may have twisting, or cracking, or a small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is only for moving by hand, but with the help of subsequent remedies that come hereafter, and then holds tightly at this moment subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And that the fracture which is coming on horseback, and are the two joints dislocated, they must now set them levelly so that splintered pieces stand out.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if chalk is applied to it when they come, let them not leave any night until the application of the chalk has calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then place it gently where you can move and massage it back into position, ensuring that its repair is lighter than the treatments for them or they have fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then restrain, as he will afterwards require it to.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if it concerns the bone in pieces, when two parts are needed—by hand or tool (possibly indicating instruments for splinting), or small limbs and cords/strings involved, wherein your hands may be required:

et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And properly align the two ends of the bones according to their best forms.

et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And keep it correctly aligned so that any twisting does not occur while they are in recovery.

Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality required for piercing through bone is to place the cautery on the bone and return it as long as you see that the bone has been penetrated.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put back the cautery somewhere afterward, and so proceed accordingly, then use your incisors to work on the space within the bone where they meet, doing it more subtly than you can manage, carefully and precisely as we have instructed, continuing until you handle the bone with your hand or any of the extremities like nails.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And make sure not to disturb the brain nor the spinal cord (sfac). This line advises caution regarding bodily structures that should be avoided during self-treatment
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone set and worked on it with tools resembling an incisor but required to be more delicately handled than any other such instrument, they must indeed strive for even greater care and subtlety. Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	He must first discover the broken part of the bone, whether that be above or below where it has fractured openly; once discovered therein, he places his lance-like cutting instrument accordingly shaped by its form. (Note: "lenticulaire" refers to a lens shape here)
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And does not cut into one side or the other but toward the bone itself. (Note: The original text seems to be discussing a technique where only direct action towards the fractured part is made.)
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then with a small mallet, carefully hammer the bone throughout its entirety, and be mindful of where you are working on.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is within the bone, hammer carefully for its well-being and to prevent harm or fear.

de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Whenever the shoulder breaks or becomes loose, it moves within its socket, only by means of contact.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If the apparatus conforms to the shape of the breakage, and reset it according to its natural form in all ways you can manage.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then apply powder from the mill with plenty of oil, and sprinkle lightly, and place under two coverings.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place on a slender and wide iron plate slightly wider than the shoulder blade, securing it with any part of the arm bone that does not move in its joint. If using hair from arrows as padding for the edge of the iron plate, ensure it sits evenly without movement at all points where the armbone is immobile.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then tightly bind it firmly so that the iron plate does not move from its place, and observe each day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time if it is stretched and its axis goes out of place from where it belongs, the patient feels pain on their chest.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is reset after XX years or after XXV days.

de la brisure dou pis	of the broken piece or shard  
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is never broken by itself within it but occurs here.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but often breaks due to misuse or force applied externally.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken inside, if decay ensues therein; the patient experiences great pain and failure of alignment both internally (within) and externally (on its surface), often vomiting blood as a result, leading to exposed bone in fractured areas which causes intense discomfort.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration must be such that patients experience relief through both their hands and cussing between shoulder blades before pressing down on shoulders together with your own hands to assemble lower ribs into various positions. Continue this delicate maneuver until the bone's appearance aligns as it should;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place on springs and screws above the subtle staples of salt or another metal, and wrap it in a linen bandage under the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And turn the bandage round his back, and apply pressure again for several hours until it softens. If necessary to continue applying pressure.

de la brisure des costes	Of the fracturing of bones
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	When the fracture of the ribs occurs only in large ones after the back, and at the neck joint, they bend only because they are moist.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and feel well upon inquiry about it all.

Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who advise say that it should be administered with foods that swell the belly, to put aside indigestion.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make such things except for when chalk sticks come to us.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes from the sick or ill person.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And none of them put bandages on to heal it, and that seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt as though the bandage draws out unnecessary fluids from around the joint for its delicate positioning.

And none of them covered the joint with moist linen dipped in hot oil and inserted between the ribs to ease a cough treatment involving pus, meat, and medicinal remedies.

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the hipbone's bone

de la brisure du bras	Regarding breakage of the arm:    
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones called the "phalanges", wherein one is small and serves as this socket.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and others are large, and it is this one small toy.

Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	Whenever the little flints are broken, repairs and healing take place.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the great ones are broken, if it is in need of extensive repairing, more shards than those that were assembled together remain for a long time.

de la brisure de la main	of the breakage of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	When there are fractures on the back of our hands and arms only fall many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, they must cross their fingers and set them straight in front too.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then places its hand on the extended sleeve and extends their bones out straightly, as long as they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And places the plaster and splints upon them when needed, then puts a pin according to the amount of lead.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and is wrapped in one sheet of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is within the plant's abdomen, makes a cloth of linen and commands the patient to stretch it out in their limb.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And then a long linen bandage is used, and the pin or pincet should be as large as the bone of their hand, which they are stretched out to fit accordingly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is open to air, you must place a pin above it and another below in the foot, so that the hands are elevated and straightened out; then bind the wound tightly around both feet, securing the bandage firmly between them.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to any of us within our grasp, and it is swolthy (bulky or difficult), you must keep it as still until it seems necessary.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and with their foot pressed down, and if you see a straight small stick to lift the fragment, do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if it is with the other in index or one of them and their limb steady which comes after.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	Hold all together tightly as if they were in a basket, or placed on an iron stand similarly.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	Take warmth for restoration and proper positioning of hot abscesses, and secure what comes to it as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the bone fracture
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the shoulder is often fractured, and one can see it when they turn forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And if there lies between the breakage above or below;
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And if patients suffer on their face, then several attendants extend his/her limb evenly.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And this happens when there is a break in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And when there is a fracture near the root of the shoulder blade, one ligament attaches to the joint, and the others are attached along the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And if it is nearing its time at the knee joint, and nowhere are there ligaments around the knee or any dorsiflexion.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then place the bone on its two hands as naturally and then put in the splint, and that will be where it comes back to rest.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if it has become warm, leave it to calm down before returning to your work and treatment plan.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The splint is made in such manner (implying that there's an implied method of making the splint mentioned
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It should be wrapped in layers of strong linen or wool (I and II), removing any superfluous material, then twist the leg so that the heel edges meet at the calf's root, and pass a long thread through beneath the knee beside the groin; tie down top threads above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn it over on the leg and kneecap, then place a pin on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then use the eight between the leg and the kneecap padding to make it even, then begin with linking three turns or two above the breakage.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you move further up from the breakage, reduce the tightness.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take two threads that you have wound between the leg and kneecap padding, with three eyes above them, then return to wind at the head of the thread, as long as you see beyond the pièce (the bone), which in this context likely refers to a treatment involving close observation or adjustment near where tendons meet the bones.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And tighten until it no longer moves from its place; then leave it as is unless it swells or shows any other signs of distress.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it slips away, then direct him to whoever comes along, just as we have said many times before.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if he has bone fragments that prick, whether or not he can bear it upwards;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	And if they cannot, then it will need to be cut open and drained.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and as we have said, so long as he is made healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And no bone should be broken herein when it's set, just as in the shoulder and arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Nevertheless, nothing bothers the patient upon such restoration being made thereafter.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And whether or not a bone is restored within the year, less than that time, more than it, according to their various constitutions.

de la brisure de la jambe	of the breakdown of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	When two bones meet in the leg, one is called by right "mouton," and the others are called "fox.

de la brisure des os dou piet	of bone fractures in painful places.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle it does not come from fractures but bone misalignments and too much movement can worsen conditions for many people. The text instructs caution with movements to avoid exacerbating any potential injuries, particularly in cases where there is already pain or a threat of further harm due to incorrect handling.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it occurs that the bones are broken and you see these moving against each other, as painful flesh moves on earthly grounds or when they fly upwards like birds in their claws, then place your finger under them carefully. Lift until you feel resistance from within those places; press down with firm pressure till relief is felt into the affected areas of limb—thereby addressing both bone displacement and accompanying discomfort or pain according to medieval practices described herein for healing misalignments associated with fractures.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier. Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are none to break them up, restore them back in accordance with what we have said is the proper way of handling bones by hand.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place an iron fragment according to the length of that piece I mentioned earlier and make it slightly larger than necessary before inserting into the socket. Then apply pressure with this tool for alignment.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if it's two or three pieces found therein, break them off accordingly and wrap each in a single layer of linen. et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if it is stuck at the head of the shoulder against the chest when dirtied.

de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	from the fracture of the bone in the joint,   
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of nature is broken in women and if flesh swells upwards, then incline it towards the back part, and hold it by the rear.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the sling with the natural fiber of the patient's linen, and put in as much thickness as I.

et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she urinates, if her linen compresses (indicating the need to adjust for moisture), and when she voids again, reset it, continuing this process as long as seven years or so. This iterative approach emphasizes caution with recurrences of dislocation due possibly to wet conditions that could exacerbate such injuries in medieval times without modern medical interventions.

This suggests an age-old practice where traditional beliefs about using certain animals' products for healing were prevalent before the understanding of modern medicine became widespread.

la nature si revenra li brisure;	The injury may recur back then.

li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand

Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And if it is seen that the ankle has swelled up, attempt to address at the part where it's dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And if ligament damage is present and must be stretched with his hands when he can move somewhat comfortably.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is set down in its place entirely, then you must make the patient lie with his back against us and use their leg to hold him up above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then take the piece with your right hand, and then again with your left, twice in total, lift it upward, and firmly hold the piece high.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	And do this two times as we have said, hammering and taking the piece.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that is good enough.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	But if it starts over again, because it comes back.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot return like this, then fix the patient on their back against the ground with your left hand firmly in the groin area between their legs. Keep a strong grip and hold tight so that the patient does not sweat.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then you bleach or clean the groin area (possibly with urine), and other ministers extend the piece to his hands or ties it around the back of the pelvis where it rests on his spine.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then servants extend gently, and the instrument is placed between the joints of the patient to hold them in place.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place an uneven pressure on the dislocated joint and apply other agents of decay to the healthy leg, causing the dislocation to return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at rest, if you apply the splint and secure them in place on the leg, making sure that the straps do not cross too tightly over the knee joints behind.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then he leaves it for two or three days if strained.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then he allows him to lie down at noon or quarter past until the ill person is cured over four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if it advances further, that's not to be ensured unless he continues the treatment even now.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes at nightfall, you must soothe it as we have said elsewhere while still healthy.

Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the joint is reduced and they find it comfortable to extend their arm or limb, that's a light task at hand for work. These instructions likely relate to traditional medical practices of medieval times dealing with musculosthy dislocations as outlined in an old French treat
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if dislocations occur at any point on the back or spine, they must be made to sit up straight upon their knees or flat surface, and place your hand under these joints, then press firmly until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is immobile and does not open at all, place the foot on two legs of a table then form them tightly, leave it for three days, then release.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him rest until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When injury comes with dislocation, it is often seen that the patients die.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not careful in the treatment and if you do not have skill in it for a long time, and if you lack pity and mercy, and delay is your habit, then never bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And start with soothing warm applications first, leaving the patient holding a dove unless you see hope for health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, if now restores the limb to its place so that the apathexis flesh can heal.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when parts are in the locked position, if you apply cooling agents immediately and treat any wounds as needed with such ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and with dislocation comes breakage, if small bones are involved, and as we have done in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and avoid entering the path of fear as I have instructed you, for it is by your Maker's provision that you move and are equipped with weapons or armor.
